## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Materials Science / Constitutive Modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the temperature-dependent stress-strain relationship of solids, a core problem in materials science and solid mechanics. It captures elastic-plastic deformation, strain hardening, and thermal softening effects governed by dislocation dynamics and thermodynamic principles.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic: sigma = (c0 - c1 * T) * epsilon (temperature-dependent Young's modulus)
- Ludwik power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (dynamic recovery saturation)
- Johnson-Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (separable strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Thermal activation scaling: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (thermally assisted dislocation motion)
- Zerilli-Armstrong type: sigma = c0 + c1 * sqrt(epsilon) + c2 * T * sqrt(epsilon) (BCC/FCC metal dislocation theory)
- Polynomial-T coupling: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * (1 - c3 * T) (higher-order strain with linear thermal softening)
- Dual-stage hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (low and high strain regimes)
- Rational strain saturation: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * epsilon) (asymptotic flow stress limit)
- Power-law thermal dependence: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (empirical high-temperature flow scaling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Plastic strain hardening → Power-law epsilon**c or Voce saturation 1 - exp(-c * epsilon)
- Thermal softening → Multiplicative linear decay (c0 - c1 * T) or exponential scaling exp(-c * T) on strain function
- Elastic-plastic smooth transition → epsilon * (1 - exp(-c * epsilon)) or polynomial blending epsilon + c * epsilon**2
- Dislocation density strengthening → Square-root dependence sqrt(epsilon) (Taylor hardening relation)
- Dual hardening mechanisms (storage + recovery) → Additive combination c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) + c2 * epsilon**c3
- Temperature-driven yield drop → Linear thermal offset c0 - c1 * T independent of strain
- High-temperature flow scaling → Coupled power-law epsilon**c1 * T**c2
- Phase transformation softening → Sigmoidal temperature modulation tanh(c * (T - c0)) or rational 1 / (1 + c * T)

Wait, I might have missed something. Let's re-read the GT carefully.
GT: `c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*(T - c7)*sin(epsilon)`
= `c0*epsilon*(-c1*T + c1*c2 + c3) + c4*epsilon**3 + c6*T*sin(epsilon) - c6*c7*sin(epsilon)`
= `(-c0*c1) * epsilon * T + (c0*c1*c2 + c0*c3) * epsilon + c4 * epsilon**3 + c6 * T * sin(epsilon) - c6*c7 * sin(epsilon)`

Basis functions: `epsilon*T`, `epsilon`, `epsilon**3`, `T*sin(epsilon)`, `sin(epsilon)`.

Let's check Candidate 41 again: `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**3 + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*sin(c5*log(c6*epsilon + 1) + c7)`
It has `T*epsilon`, `epsilon**3`, `epsilon`. But the sine term is `sin(c5*log(...) + c7)`. This cannot match `T*sin(epsilon)` or `sin(epsilon)`. So NO MATCH.

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*(T - c7)*sin(epsilon)`

Expanding and grouping by basis functions of `epsilon` and `T`:
`GT = (-c0*c1) * epsilon * T + (c0*c1*c2 + c0*c3) * epsilon + c4 * epsilon**3 + c6 * T * sin(epsilon) - c6*c7 * sin(epsilon)`

Given the fixed numerical values (`c5=3.0`, `c6≠0`, `c7≠0`), the GT is a strict linear combination of exactly five linearly independent basis functions:
1. `epsilon * T`
2. `epsilon`
3. `epsilon**3`
4. `T * sin(epsilon)`
5. `sin(epsilon)`

Any mathematically equivalent candidate must be able to form these exact five basis functions through algebraic manipulation and constant assignment. We will evaluate each candidate against this requirement.
